</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a></th>
<td><span lang="por">Região Administrativa Especial de Macau<br/>
<small>(for "Macau Special Administrative Region")</small><br/>
<small>pronounced </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[ʁɨʒiˈɐ̃w̃ ɐdminiʃtɾɐˈtivɐ (ɨ)ʃpɨsiˈaɫ dɨ mɐˈkaw]</a></span></span></td>
</tr>
<tr style="display:none">
<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Macau</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">aʊ</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Macau.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/df/En-ca-Macau.oga" title="En-ca-Macau.oga">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>), also spelled <b>Macao</b> and officially the <b>Macao Special Administrative Region of the People's Republic of China</b>, is an autonomous region on the western side of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_(China)" title="Pearl River (China)">Pearl River</a> <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>. Macau is bordered by the city of <a href="/wiki/Zhuhai" title="Zhuhai">Zhuhai</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">Mainland China</a> to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">Pearl River Delta</a> to the east and south. <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> lies about 64 kilometres (40 mi) to its east across the Delta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M475_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-M475-9">[5]</a></sup> With a population of 650,900<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census2016_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-census2016-6">[3]</a></sup> living in an area of 30.5 km<sup>2</sup> (11.8 sq mi), it is the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" title="List of countries by population density">densely populated region</a> in the world. A former <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> colony, it was returned to Chinese sovereignty on 20 December 1999.</p>
<p>Macau was administered by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> and its inheritor states from the mid-16th century until late 1999, when it constituted the last remaining European colony in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[7]</a></sup> Portuguese traders first settled in Macau in the 1550s. In 1557, <a href="/wiki/Luso-Chinese_agreement_(1554)" title="Luso-Chinese agreement (1554)">Macau was leased to Portugal</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming China</a> as a trading port. The Portuguese Empire administered the city under Chinese authority and sovereignty until 1887, when Macau became a colony through a mutual agreement between the two countries. Sovereignty over Macau was <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Macau" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Macau">transferred back to China on 20 December 1999</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Declaration_on_the_Question_of_Macau" title="Joint Declaration on the Question of Macau">Joint Declaration on the Question of Macau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macau_Basic_Law" title="Macau Basic Law">Macau Basic Law</a> stipulate that Macau operate with a high degree of autonomy until at least 2049, fifty years after the transfer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blm_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-blm-12">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Under the policy of "<a href="/wiki/One_country,_two_systems" title="One country, two systems">one country, two systems</a>", the <a href="/wiki/State_Council_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="State Council of the People's Republic of China">State Council of the People's Republic of China</a> is responsible for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_Macau_Garrison" title="People's Liberation Army Macau Garrison">military defense</a> and foreign affairs while Macau maintains its own <a href="/wiki/Legal_system_of_Macau" title="Legal system of Macau">legal system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_Security_Police_Force_of_Macau" title="Public Security Police Force of Macau">public security force</a>, monetary system, customs policy and <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Macau" title="Immigration to Macau">immigration policy</a>. Macau participates in international organizations and events that do not require members to possess national sovereignty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blm_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-blm-12">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Macau is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resort_city" title="Resort city">resort city</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_China" title="Southern China">Southern China</a>, known for its casinos and luxury hotels. Its gaming revenue has been the world's largest since 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[10]</a></sup> with the economy heavily dependent on gaming and tourism. According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Factbook</a></i>, Macau has the fourth highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-life_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-life-15">[11]</a></sup> Moreover, it has a very high <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, ranking 18th in the world as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_in_Figures.2C_2016_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_in_Figures.2C_2016-16">[12]</a></sup> Macau is among the world's richest regions and as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> its <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP per capita by purchasing power parity is higher</a> than that of any country in the world, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is widely known as the pre-eminent gambling (or gaming) capital of the world, greatly dwarfing other gambling centers/cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Macau" title="Names of Macau">Names of Macau</a></div>
<p>The present Chinese name (Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hant">澳門</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Àomén</span></i>; Cantonese Yale: <i><span lang="yue">Oumún</span></i>) means "Bay Outlet". Macau is otherwise known in Chinese as <i>Haojing</i> (<span lang="zh-hant">濠鏡</span>, literally "Oyster Mirror") or <i>Jinghai</i> (<span lang="zh-hant">鏡海</span>, literally "Mirror Sea").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M517_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-M517-21">[17]</a></sup> The name <i>Macau</i> is thought to be derived from the <i><a href="/wiki/A-Ma_Temple" title="A-Ma Temple">A-Ma Temple</a></i> (Chinese: <span lang="zh-Hant">媽閣廟</span>; pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Māgé Miào</span></i>; Cantonese Yale: <i><span lang="yue">Māgok Miuh</span></i>), a temple built in 1448 dedicated to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mazu_(goddess)" title="Mazu (goddess)">Mazu</a>, the goddess of seafarers and fishermen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[18]</a></sup> More precisely, the name <i>Macau</i> corresponds to the Chinese name "<span lang="zh-hant">媽港</span>" (pinyin: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Magang</span></i>), meaning "Harbor of Mazu", and referring to the waters adjacent to the Ama Temple.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Macau" title="History of Macau">History of Macau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macau" title="Portuguese Macau">Portuguese Macau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Macau" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Macau">Transfer of sovereignty over Macau</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saopaulo_Chinnery.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="384" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Saopaulo_Chinnery.jpg/220px-Saopaulo_Chinnery.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Saopaulo_Chinnery.jpg/330px-Saopaulo_Chinnery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ca/Saopaulo_Chinnery.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saopaulo_Chinnery.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ruins of São Paulo Cathedral, built in 1602 and destroyed by fire in 1835</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The history of Macau is traced back to the <a href="/wiki/Qin_dynasty" title="Qin dynasty">Qin dynasty</a> (221–206 BC), when the region now called Macau came under the jurisdiction of Panyu County, Nanhai Prefecture (modern <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M517_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-M517-21">[17]</a></sup> The first recorded Chinese inhabitants of the area were people seeking refuge in Macau from invading <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Song" title="Southern Song">Southern Song</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_history_in_Macau_encyclopedia_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_history_in_Macau_encyclopedia-24">[20]</a></sup> Under the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> (1368–1644), fishermen migrated to Macau from Guangdong and <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>. The Macau native people were <a href="/wiki/Tanka_people" title="Tanka people">Tanka</a> boat people.</p>
<p>Macau did not develop as a major settlement until the Portuguese arrived in the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[21]</a></sup> In 1513, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_%C3%81lvares" title="Jorge Álvares">Jorge Álvares</a> became the first Portuguese to land in China. In 1535, Portuguese traders obtained the rights to anchor ships in Macau's harbours and to carry out trading activities, though not the right to stay onshore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[22]</a></sup> Around 1552–1553, they obtained temporary permission to erect storage sheds onshore, in order to dry out goods drenched by sea water;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-F7_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-F7-27">[23]</a></sup> they soon built rudimentary stone houses around the area now called Nam Van.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_Macau">Portuguese Macau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Portuguese Macau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:200_Escudos_comm%C3%A9morant_l%27arriv%C3%A9e_des_Portugais_en_Chine_en_1513,_pi%C3%A8ce_frapp%C3%A9e_en_1996.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="591" data-file-width="1200" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/200_Escudos_comm%C3%A9morant_l%27arriv%C3%A9e_des_Portugais_en_Chine_en_1513%2C_pi%C3%A8ce_frapp%C3%A9e_en_1996.jpg/220px-200_Escudos_comm%C3%A9morant_l%27arriv%C3%A9e_des_Portugais_en_Chine_en_1513%2C_pi%C3%A8ce_frapp%C3%A9e_en_1996.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/200_Escudos_comm%C3%A9morant_l%27arriv%C3%A9e_des_Portugais_en_Chine_en_1513%2C_pi%C3%A8ce_frapp%C3%A9e_en_1996.jpg/330px-200_Escudos_comm%C3%A9morant_l%27arriv%C3%A9e_des_Portugais_en_Chine_en_1513%2C_pi%C3%A8ce_frapp%C3%A9e_en_1996.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/200_Escudos_comm%C3%A9morant_l%27arriv%C3%A9e_des_Portugais_en_Chine_en_1513%2C_pi%C3%A8ce_frapp%C3%A9e_en_1996.jpg/440px-200_Escudos_comm%C3%A9morant_l%27arriv%C3%A9e_des_Portugais_en_Chine_en_1513%2C_pi%C3%A8ce_frapp%C3%A9e_en_1996.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:200_Escudos_comm%C3%A9morant_l%27arriv%C3%A9e_des_Portugais_en_Chine_en_1513,_pi%C3%A8ce_frapp%C3%A9e_en_1996.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portuguese coin (minted 1996) commemorating the arrival of the Portuguese in China in 1513</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1557, the Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Luso-Chinese_agreement_(1554)" title="Luso-Chinese agreement (1554)">established a permanent settlement in Macau</a>, paying an annual rent of 500 <a href="/wiki/Tael" title="Tael">taels</a> (18.9 <a href="/wiki/Kilogram" title="Kilogram">kilograms</a> / 41.6 <a href="/wiki/Pound_(mass)" title="Pound (mass)">pounds</a>) of silver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-F7_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-F7-27">[23]</a></sup> The Portuguese continued to pay an annual tribute up to 1863 in order to stay in Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1564, Portugal commanded western trade with <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, and China. In 1631 the Chinese restricted Portuguese commerce in China to the port of Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 17th century, some 5,000 slaves lived in Macau, in addition to 2,000 Portuguese and 20,000 Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>As more Portuguese settled in Macau to engage in trade, they made demands for self-administration; but this was not achieved until the 1840s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[29]</a></sup> In 1576, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Gregory_XIII" title="Pope Gregory XIII">Pope Gregory XIII</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Macau" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Macau">Roman Catholic Diocese of Macau</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[30]</a></sup> In 1583, the Portuguese in Macau were permitted to form a Senate to handle various issues concerning their social and economic affairs under strict supervision of the Chinese authority,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[31]</a></sup> but there was no transfer of sovereignty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_history_in_Macau_encyclopedia_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_history_in_Macau_encyclopedia-24">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1870Macao.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="240" data-file-width="360" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/1870Macao.jpg/220px-1870Macao.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/1870Macao.jpg/330px-1870Macao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/1870Macao.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1870Macao.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Macau, c. 1870</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Macau prospered as a port but it was the target of repeated failed attempts<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[32]</a></sup> by the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> to conquer it in the 17th century. On 24 June 1622, the Dutch attacked Macau in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Macau" title="Battle of Macau">Battle of Macau</a>, in the hope of turning it into a Dutch possession. The Portuguese repulsed their attack and the Dutch never tried to conquer Macau again. The majority of the defenders were African slaves, with only a few Portuguese soldiers and priests. Captain Kornelis Reyerszoon was commander of the 800-strong Dutch invasion force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The grieving Dutch Governor <a href="/wiki/Jan_Pieterszoon_Coen" title="Jan Pieterszoon Coen">Jan Pz. Coen</a> said after the defeat that "The slaves of the Portuguese at Macau served them so well and faithfully, that it was they who defeated and drove away our people there last year", and "Our people saw very few Portuguese" during the battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a> (1839–42), Portugal occupied the empty islands of <a href="/wiki/Taipa" title="Taipa">Taipa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coloane" title="Coloane">Coloane</a> in 1851 and 1864 respectively. On 1 December 1887, the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing</a> and Portuguese governments signed the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Portuguese_Treaty_of_Peking" title="Sino-Portuguese Treaty of Peking">Sino-Portuguese Treaty of Peking</a>, under which China ceded the right of "perpetual occupation and government of Macau by Portugal" in compliance with the statements of the Protocol of Lisbon. In return, Macau Government would cooperate with Hong Kong's smuggling trade in Indian opium and China would profit from imposing customs taxes. Portugal was also obliged "never to alienate Macau without previous agreement with China", therefore ensuring that negotiation between Portugal and France (regarding a possible exchange of Macau and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a> with the <a href="/wiki/French_Congo" title="French Congo">French Congo</a>) or with other countries would not go forward – so that the British commercial interests would be secured; Macau officially became a territory under Portuguese administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_history_in_Macau_encyclopedia_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_history_in_Macau_encyclopedia-24">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MacauPortoInterior1900.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="207" data-file-width="300" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/MacauPortoInterior1900.jpg/220px-MacauPortoInterior1900.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/MacauPortoInterior1900.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MacauPortoInterior1900.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "O Porto Interior" in Macau, c. 1900</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1928, after the Qing dynasty had been overthrown following the <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) government officially notified Portugal that it would abrogate the Treaty of Amity and Commerce;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M518_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-M518-45">[41]</a></sup> the two powers signed a new Sino-Portuguese Friendship and Trade Treaty in place of the abrogated treaty. Changing only a few provisions concerning tariff principles and matters relating to business affairs, the new treaty did not alter the sovereignty of Macau and Portuguese government of Macau remained unchanged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, unlike <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">Portuguese Timor</a>, which was occupied by the Japanese in 1942 along with <a href="/wiki/West_Timor" title="West Timor">Dutch Timor</a>, the Japanese respected Portuguese neutrality in Macau, but only up to a point. Macau enjoyed a brief period of economic prosperity as the only neutral port in <a href="/wiki/South_China" title="South China">South China</a> after the Japanese had occupied Guangzhou and Hong Kong. In August 1943, Japanese troops seized the British steamer <i>Sian</i> in Macau and killed about 20 guards. The next month they demanded the installation of Japanese "advisors" under the threat of overt military occupation. The result was that a virtual Japanese <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> was created over Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garrett.2C_p._116_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Garrett.2C_p._116-47">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>When it was discovered that "neutral" Macau was planning to sell aviation fuel to Japan, aircraft from the <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(CV-6)" title="USS Enterprise (CV-6)">USS <i>Enterprise</i></a> bombed and strafed the hangar of the Naval Aviation Centre on 16 January 1945 to destroy the fuel. American air raids on targets in Macau were also made on 25 February and 11 June 1945. Following Portuguese government protests, in 1950 the United States paid US$20,255,952 to the government of Portugal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garrett.2C_p._116_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Garrett.2C_p._116-47">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between the end of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a> and the establishment of the People's Republic of China, Macau served as a safe haven for refugees of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the establishment of the People's Republic of China in 1949, the Beijing government declared the Sino-Portuguese Treaty invalid as an "<a href="/wiki/Unequal_treaty" title="Unequal treaty">unequal treaty</a>" imposed by foreigners on China. However, Beijing was not ready to settle the treaty question, allowing the maintenance of "the status quo" until a more appropriate time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a> in mainland China and by general dissatisfaction with Portuguese government, riots broke out in Macau in 1966. In the most serious, the so-called <a href="/wiki/12-3_incident" title="12-3 incident">12-3 incident</a>, 6 people were killed and more than 200 people were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lo_Shiu-hing_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lo_Shiu-hing-50">[46]</a></sup> On 28 January 1967, the Portuguese government issued a formal apology by means of an "admission of guilt".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after Portugal's 1974 <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a>, which overthrew the <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo dictatorship</a>, the new government determined it would relinquish all its overseas possessions. In 1976, Lisbon redefined Macau as a "Chinese territory under Portuguese administration" and granted it a large measure of administrative, financial, and economic autonomy. Three years later, Portugal and China agreed to regard Macau as "a Chinese territory under [temporary] Portuguese administration".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[48]</a></sup> The Chinese and Portuguese governments commenced negotiations on the question of Macau in June 1986. The two signed the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Declaration_on_the_Question_of_Macau" title="Joint Declaration on the Question of Macau">Sino-Portuguese Joint Declaration</a> the next year, making Macau one of the <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_regions_of_China" title="Special administrative regions of China">special administrative regions of China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transfer_of_sovereignty_and_SAR_status">Transfer of sovereignty and SAR status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Transfer of sovereignty and SAR status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Chinese government <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Macau" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Macau">assumed formal sovereignty over Macau</a> on 20 December 1999 as a <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_regions_of_China" title="Special administrative regions of China">special administrative region</a> (SAR) after over 400 years of Portuguese colonial rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[50]</a></sup> This event also marked the end of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> and European colonialism in Asia. The economy since then has continued to prosper with the sustained growth of tourism from <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> and the construction of new <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casinos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Macau" title="Politics of Macau">Politics of Macau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Macau" title="Legislative Assembly of Macau">Legislative Assembly of Macau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legal_system_of_Macau" title="Legal system of Macau">Legal system of Macau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Civic_and_Municipal_Affairs_Bureau" title="Civic and Municipal Affairs Bureau">Civic and Municipal Affairs Bureau</a></div>
<p>The Sino-Portuguese Joint Declaration and Macau Basic Law, Macau's constitution, promulgated by China's <a href="/wiki/National_People%27s_Congress" title="National People's Congress">National People's Congress</a> in 1993, specify that Macau's social and economic system, lifestyle, rights, and freedoms are to remain unchanged for at least 50 years after the transfer of sovereignty to China in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blm_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-blm-12">[8]</a></sup> Under the principle of "one country, two systems", Macau enjoys a high degree of autonomy in all areas except defence and foreign affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blm_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-blm-12">[8]</a></sup> Macau officials, rather than PRC officials, run Macau through the exercise of separate executive, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative" title="Legislative">legislative</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial" title="Judicial">judicial</a> powers, as well as the right to final adjudication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[53]</a></sup> Macau maintains its own currency (the <a href="/wiki/Macanese_pataca" title="Macanese pataca">Macanese pataca</a>), customs territory, immigration and border controls and police force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive">Executive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Executive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macau_Government_Headquarters_01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Macau_Government_Headquarters_01.JPG/220px-Macau_Government_Headquarters_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Macau_Government_Headquarters_01.JPG/330px-Macau_Government_Headquarters_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Macau_Government_Headquarters_01.JPG/440px-Macau_Government_Headquarters_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macau_Government_Headquarters_01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Macau_Government_Headquarters" title="Macau Government Headquarters">Macau Government Headquarters</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The government in Macau is headed by the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Executive_of_Macau" title="Chief Executive of Macau">Chief Executive of Macau</a>, who is appointed by the central government upon the recommendation of an election committee, whose three hundred members are nominated by corporate and community bodies. The recommendation is made by an election within the committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[56]</a></sup> The chief executive's cabinet is made up of five policy secretaries and is advised by the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_Macau" title="Executive Council of Macau">Executive Council of Macau</a>, which has between seven and eleven members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_2007_Yearbook_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_2007_Yearbook-61">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Ho" title="Edmund Ho">Edmund Ho</a>, a community leader and former banker, was the first chief executive of the Macau SAR, replacing <a href="/wiki/Vasco_Joaquim_Rocha_Vieira" title="Vasco Joaquim Rocha Vieira">General Vasco Rocha Vieira</a> at midnight on 20 December 1999. <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Chui" title="Fernando Chui">Fernando Chui</a> is the current Chief Executive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[58]</a></sup> The chief executive and the cabinet have their offices in the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Government_Headquarters" title="Macau Government Headquarters">Macau Government Headquarters</a>, located in the area of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o,_Macau" title="São Lourenço, Macau">São Lourenço</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislature">Legislature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Legislature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Assembleia_Legislativa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2560" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Assembleia_Legislativa.jpg/220px-Assembleia_Legislativa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Assembleia_Legislativa.jpg/330px-Assembleia_Legislativa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Assembleia_Legislativa.jpg/440px-Assembleia_Legislativa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Assembleia_Legislativa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Macau" title="Legislative Assembly of Macau">Legislative Assembly of Macau</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The legislative organ of the territory is the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Macau" title="Legislative Assembly of Macau">Legislative Assembly</a>, a 33-member body comprising 14 directly elected members, 12 indirectly elected members representing <a href="/wiki/Functional_constituency_(Macau)" title="Functional constituency (Macau)">functional constituencies</a> and seven members appointed by the chief executive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[59]</a></sup> Any permanent residents at or over 18 years of age are eligible to vote in direct elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[60]</a></sup> Indirect election is limited to organizations registered as "corporate voters" and a 300-member election committee drawn from broad regional groupings, municipal organizations, and central government bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2009, the Legislative Assembly passed the <a href="/wiki/Macau_national_security_law" title="Macau national security law">Macau national security law</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Basic_Law_Article_23" title="Hong Kong Basic Law Article 23">a withdrawn security legislation</a> previously introduced in Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[62]</a></sup> Democracy advocates feared that the bill's excessively broad scope could lead to abuses, a concern which has been heightened after a number of prominent supporters of democracy in Hong Kong <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Macau_cultural_exchange" title="Hong Kong Macau cultural exchange">were denied entry</a> into Macau in the run-up to the bill's passage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EdfDosTribunaisDeSegundaEUltimaInstancias1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/EdfDosTribunaisDeSegundaEUltimaInstancias1.jpg/220px-EdfDosTribunaisDeSegundaEUltimaInstancias1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/EdfDosTribunaisDeSegundaEUltimaInstancias1.jpg/330px-EdfDosTribunaisDeSegundaEUltimaInstancias1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/EdfDosTribunaisDeSegundaEUltimaInstancias1.jpg/440px-EdfDosTribunaisDeSegundaEUltimaInstancias1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EdfDosTribunaisDeSegundaEUltimaInstancias1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seat of the Superior Tribunal of Macau</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The original framework of the legal system, based largely on the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Portugal" title="Law of Portugal">Law of Portugal</a>, the Portuguese civil law system, was preserved after 1999. The territory has its own independent judicial system with a <a href="/wiki/High_Court" title="High Court">High Court</a>. Judges are selected by a committee and appointed by the chief executive. Foreign judges may serve on the courts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Macau has a three-tier court system: the Court of the First Instance, the Court of the Second Instance and the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Final_Appeal_(Macau)" title="Court of Final Appeal (Macau)">Court of Final Appeal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Legal_System_of_Macau_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Legal_System_of_Macau-69">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_Macau_Garrison" title="People's Liberation Army Macau Garrison">People's Liberation Army Macau Garrison</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Macau_under_Portuguese_rule" title="Military of Macau under Portuguese rule">Military of Macau under Portuguese rule</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liaison_Office_of_the_Central_People%27s_Government_in_the_Macao_Special_Administrative_Region" title="Liaison Office of the Central People's Government in the Macao Special Administrative Region">Liaison Office of the Central People's Government in the Macao Special Administrative Region</a></div>
<p>Under Portuguese rule, Macau often served as an expeditionary base to <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and other regions of East Asia from the 16th century onwards, while maintaining a strong garrison mainly to repel Dutch and mainland Chinese attacks. However, since the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Portuguese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Portuguese Alliance">allied</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> settled Hong Kong, the need for a strong military presence in Macau dimmed and it became limited before ceasing in 1974. However, despite having no Portuguese garrison left on the territory, a small security force managed by the local <a href="/wiki/Pol%C3%ADcia_de_Seguran%C3%A7a_P%C3%BAblica" title="Polícia de Segurança Pública">PSP</a> was kept, which proved useful with the escalating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triad_(underground_society)" title="Triad (underground society)">triad</a> warfare tensions towards the last decades of Portuguese administration. Also the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_of_the_Port" title="Captain of the Port">Capitania dos Portos</a> kept operating a coast guard and the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Armed_Forces" title="Portuguese Armed Forces">Portuguese airforce</a> kept airfields active until the opening of <a href="/wiki/Macau_International_Airport" title="Macau International Airport">Macau International Airport</a> in the mid-1990s. In 1999, upon handover to the PRC, a substantial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_Macau_Garrison" title="People's Liberation Army Macau Garrison">garrison of the People's Liberation Army</a> was established in the city helping deliver the last blow to the violence perpetrated by the triads, who were weakened by police action and arrests prior to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Handover_of_Macau_to_China" title="Handover of Macau to China">handover</a>. The garrison remains, with a large portion of the forces stationed in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Zhuhai" title="Zhuhai">Zhuhai</a> as well.</p>
<p>According to the Article 14, <a href="/wiki/Macau_Basic_Law" title="Macau Basic Law">Macau Basic Law</a>, The Central People's Government shall be responsible for the defense of the Macao Special Administrative Region. And The Government of the Macao SAR shall be responsible for the maintenance of public order in the Region.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Administrative_Division_of_Macau.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1110" height="297" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Administrative_Division_of_Macau.png/220px-Administrative_Division_of_Macau.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Administrative_Division_of_Macau.png/330px-Administrative_Division_of_Macau.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Administrative_Division_of_Macau.png/440px-Administrative_Division_of_Macau.png 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Administrative_Division_of_Macau.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Administrative divisions of Macau</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Macau is divided into 8 <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Macau" title="Parishes of Macau">parishes</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Macau" title="Geography of Macau">Geography of Macau</a></div>
<p>Macau is situated 60 kilometres (37 mi) southwest of Hong Kong and 145 kilometres (90 mi) from <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">Mainland China</a>. It also has 41 kilometres (25 mi) of coastline, yet only 310 metres (1,000 ft) of land border with <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">Mainland China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M475_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-M475-9">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asiarooms_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asiarooms-71">[67]</a></sup> It consists of the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Peninsula" title="Macau Peninsula">Macau Peninsula</a> itself and the islands of <a href="/wiki/Taipa" title="Taipa">Taipa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coloane" title="Coloane">Coloane</a>, which are now connected by landfill forming <a href="/wiki/Cotai" title="Cotai">Cotai</a>. The peninsula is formed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhu_Jiang" title="Zhu Jiang">Zhu Jiang</a> (Pearl River) <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> on the east and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xi_Jiang" title="Xi Jiang">Xi Jiang</a> (West River) on the west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asiarooms_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-Asiarooms-71">[67]</a></sup> It borders the <a href="/wiki/Zhuhai" title="Zhuhai">Zhuhai</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zone" title="Special Economic Zone">Special Economic Zone</a> in mainland China. The main border crossing between Macau and China is known as the <a href="/wiki/Portas_do_Cerco" title="Portas do Cerco">Portas do Cerco</a> (Barrier Gate) on the Macau side, and the <a href="/wiki/Gongbei_Port_of_Entry" title="Gongbei Port of Entry">Gongbei Port of Entry</a> on the Zhuhai side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup></p>

<p>Macau Peninsula was originally an island, but a connecting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandbar" title="Sandbar">sandbar</a> gradually turned into a narrow <a href="/wiki/Isthmus" title="Isthmus">isthmus</a>. Land reclamation in the 17th century transformed Macau into a peninsula with generally flat terrain, though numerous steep hills still mark the original land mass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asiarooms_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-Asiarooms-71">[67]</a></sup> Alto de Coloane is the highest point in Macau, with an altitude of 170.6 metres (559.7 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M475_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-M475-9">[5]</a></sup> With a dense <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urbanisation" title="Urbanisation">urban environment</a>, Macau has no arable land, pastures, forest, or woodland.</p>
<p>In 2015, the Chinese government assigned Macau administrative responsibility for 85 km<sup>2</sup> (33 sq mi) of coastal ocean area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-waterarea_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-waterarea-73">[69]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 1054px">
<div style="width: 1054px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Macau has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Cwa</i>), despite its low elevation coastal location south of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>, with average relative humidity between 75% and 90%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaa_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-aaa-74">[70]</a></sup> Similar to much of South China, seasonal climate is greatly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoons</a>, and differences in temperature and humidity between summer and winter are noticeable, though not as great as in mainland China. The average annual temperature of Macau is 22.7 °C (72.9 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[71]</a></sup> July is the warmest month, the average temperature being 28.9 °C (84.0 °F). The coolest month is January, with a mean temperature of 14.5 °C (58.1 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaa_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-aaa-74">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Located on China's southern coast, Macau has ample rainfall, with average annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> being 2,120 millimetres (83 in). However, winter is mostly dry due to the influence of the vast <a href="/wiki/Siberian_High" title="Siberian High">Siberian High</a> affecting much of East Asia. Autumn in Macau, from October to November, is sunny and still pleasantly warm with lower humidity. Winter (December to early March) is generally mild with temperatures above 13 °C (55 °F) most of the time, although it can drop below 8 °C (46 °F) at times. Humidity starts to increase from late March. Summer is very warm to hot (often rising above 30 °C (86 °F) during the day). The hot weather is often followed by heavy rain, thunderstorms and occasional typhoons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaa_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-aaa-74">[70]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Macau" title="Economy of Macau">Economy of Macau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gambling_in_Macau" title="Gambling in Macau">Gambling in Macau</a></div>
<table cellpadding="1" style="float: right; margin: 0 1em 1em 0; border: 1px #bbb solid; border-collapse: collapse; font-size: 90%;">
<tr style="text-align:center; background:salmon;">
<th colspan="3">Employed population by<br/>

<tr style="text-align: center;">

<td>Professionals</td>

<p>Macau's economy is based largely on tourism. Other chief economic activities in Macau are export-geared textile and garment manufacturing, banking and other financial services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C12_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-C12-80">[76]</a></sup> The clothing industry has provided about three quarters of export earnings, and the gaming, tourism and hospitality industry is estimated to contribute more than 50% of Macau's GDP, and 70% of Macau government revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_2007_Yearbook_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_2007_Yearbook-61">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Macau is a founding member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO" title="WTO">WTO</a> and has maintained sound economic and trade relations with more than 120 countries and regions, with <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Portuguese-speaking countries</a> in particular; Macau is also a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMF" title="IMF">IMF</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_factbook_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_factbook-81">[77]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> classifies Macau as a high income economy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[78]</a></sup> and the GDP per capita of the region in 2006 was US$28,436. After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_sovereignty_of_Macau" title="Transfer of the sovereignty of Macau">Handover</a> in 1999, there has been a rapid rise in the number of mainland visitors due to China's easing of travel restrictions. Together with the liberalization of Macau's gaming industry in 2001 that induces significant investment inflows, the average <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">growth rate</a> of the economy between 2001 and 2006 was approximately 13.1% annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMCMstat_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-AMCMstat-83">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a> report of international tourism for 2006, Macau ranked 21st in the number of tourists and 24th in terms of tourism receipts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[80]</a></sup> From 9.1 million visitors in 2000, arrivals to Macau has grown to 18.7 million visitors in 2005 and 22 million visitors in 2006, with over 50% of the arrivals coming from mainland China and another 30% from Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>Starting in 1962, the gambling industry had been operated under a government-issued monopoly license by <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Ho" title="Stanley Ho">Stanley Ho</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sociedade_de_Turismo_e_Divers%C3%B5es_de_Macau" title="Sociedade de Turismo e Diversões de Macau">Sociedade de Turismo e Diversões de Macau</a>. The monopoly ended in 2002 and several casino owners from <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> attempted to enter the market. With the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Sands_Macao" title="Sands Macao">Sands Macao</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sands_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-sands-86">[82]</a></sup> in 2004 and <a href="/wiki/Wynn_Macau" title="Wynn Macau">Wynn Macau</a> in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[83]</a></sup> gambling revenues from Macau's casinos grew considerably prosperous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[86]</a></sup> In 2007, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venetian_Macau" title="Venetian Macau">Venetian Macau</a>, at the time the second (in 2017 is seventh) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_buildings_in_the_world#Largest_floor_area" title="List of largest buildings in the world">largest building in the world</a> by floor area, opened its doors to the public, followed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Macau" title="MGM Grand Macau">MGM Grand Macau</a>. Numerous other hotel casinos, including <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_Macau" title="Galaxy Macau">Galaxy Cotai Megaresort</a>, opened in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[87]</a></sup> and plans for a $3.9 billion complex that will be known as Lisboa Palace is expected to be completed by 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[88]</a></sup> In February 2015, the gambling revenue in Macau fell by 48.6 percent from a year earlier to 19.5 billion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patacas" title="Patacas">patacas</a> ($2.4 billion), the biggest monthly decline that has ever been recorded. Reasons for this fall of revenue are related to the slowdown that the Chinese economy is having and a corruption crackdown by Chinese officials which has constrained lavish spending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2002, the Macau government ended the monopoly system and six casino operating concessions and subconcessions are granted to Sociedade de Turismo e Diversões de Macau, <a href="/wiki/Wynn_Resorts" title="Wynn Resorts">Wynn Resorts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Sands" title="Las Vegas Sands">Las Vegas Sands</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galaxy_entertainment" title="Galaxy entertainment">Galaxy Entertainment Group</a>, the partnership of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MGM_Mirage" title="MGM Mirage">MGM Mirage</a> and Pansy Ho (daughter of Stanley Ho), and the partnership of Melco and <a href="/wiki/Publishing_and_Broadcasting_Limited" title="Publishing and Broadcasting Limited">Publishing and Broadcasting Limited</a> (PBL). Today, there are 16 casinos operated by the STDM, and they are still crucial in the casino industry in Macau, but in 2004, the opening of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sands_Macau" title="Sands Macau">Sands Macau</a> ushered in the new era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sands_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-sands-86">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[91]</a></sup> Gambling revenue has made Macau the world's <a href="/wiki/Casino#Markets" title="Casino">top casino market</a>, surpassing Las Vegas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>The amount of performances performed in Macau has also shown an increasing trend since the early 2010s, including the show <i>House of Dancing Water</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[93]</a></sup> concerts, industry trade shows and international art crossovers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Macau is an <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">offshore financial centre</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a>, and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_port" title="Free port">free port</a> with no foreign exchange control regimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[97]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monetary_Authority_of_Macau" title="Monetary Authority of Macau">Monetary Authority of Macau</a> regulates offshore finance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[98]</a></sup> while the Macau Trade and Investment Promotion Institute provides services for investment in Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[99]</a></sup> In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Investors_Service" title="Moody's Investors Service">Moody's Investors Service</a> upgraded Macau's foreign and local currency government issuer ratings to 'Aa3' from 'A1', citing its government's solid finances as a large net creditor. The rating agency also upgraded Macau's foreign currency bank deposit ceiling to 'Aa3' from 'A1'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>As prescribed by the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Basic_Law" title="Macau Basic Law">Macau Basic Law</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Macau" title="Government of Macau">government</a> follows the principle of keeping expenditure within the limits of revenues in drawing up its budget, and strives to achieve a <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_adjustment" title="Fiscal adjustment">fiscal balance</a>, avoid <a href="/wiki/Government_budget_balance" title="Government budget balance">deficits</a> and keep the budget commensurate with the growth rate of its gross domestic product. All financial <a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">revenue</a> of the Macau Special Administrative Region shall be managed and controlled by the region itself and shall not be handed over to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Government of the People's Republic of China">Central People's Government</a>. The Central People's Government shall not levy any taxes in the Macau Special Administrative Region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLM_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-BLM-105">[101]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Monetary_system">Monetary system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Monetary system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MOP100.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="316" data-file-width="315" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/MOP100.JPG/220px-MOP100.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/97/MOP100.JPG 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MOP100.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Both sides of 100 patacas issued by BNU on 13 July 1992</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Macau, the unit of currency is the <a href="/wiki/Macanese_pataca" title="Macanese pataca">pataca</a>, which is currently pegged to the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_dollar" title="Hong Kong dollar">Hong Kong dollar</a> at a rate of HK$1 = MOP1.03.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OANDA14_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-OANDA14-106">[102]</a></sup> The name pataca is a Portuguese word which was applied to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_dollar" title="Mexican dollar">Mexican dollars</a> that were the main circulating coin in the wider region in the second half of the 19th century. In 1894, the pataca was introduced in both Macau and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">Portuguese Timor</a> as a unit of account for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_dollar" title="Mexican dollar">Mexican dollar</a> and the other silver dollar coins in circulation. However, the pataca was not the official currency when it was first enacted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OANDA14_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-OANDA14-106">[102]</a></sup> In 1901, it was decided to grant the <a href="/wiki/Banco_Nacional_Ultramarino" title="Banco Nacional Ultramarino">Banco Nacional Ultramarino</a> the exclusive rights to issue banknotes denominated in patacas, and in the year 1906, all foreign coins were outlawed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OANDA14_106-2"><a href="#cite_note-OANDA14-106">[102]</a></sup> However, the Chinese were suspicious of these paper patacas, being so accustomed to using silver for barter, and as such, the paper patacas circulated at a discount in relation to the silver dollar coins.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>In 1935, when <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> abandoned the silver standard, the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_dollar" title="Hong Kong dollar">Hong Kong dollar</a> was pegged to sterling at the fixed rate of 1 shilling and 3 pence, whereas the pataca was pegged to the Portuguese escudo at a sterling equivalent rate of only 1 shilling. From 1945 to 1951, fractional coins of the pataca were minted for issue in Portuguese Timor; and, in 1952, similar issues were minted for Macau including an actual pataca coin for the first time.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Macau" title="Demographics of Macau">Demographics of Macau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macau_people" title="Macau people">Macau people</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macau-Chinese%26Portuguese.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Macau-Chinese%26Portuguese.jpg/220px-Macau-Chinese%26Portuguese.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Macau-Chinese%26Portuguese.jpg/330px-Macau-Chinese%26Portuguese.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Macau-Chinese%26Portuguese.jpg/440px-Macau-Chinese%26Portuguese.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
</div>
<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">
