</div>
</div>
<p>Macau is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" title="List of countries by population density">most densely populated</a> region in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[104]</a></sup> with a population density of 21,185.28 persons per square kilometre in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census2016_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-census2016-6">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> make up 95% of Macau's population; another 2% is of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> and/or mixed Chinese/Portuguese descent, an ethnic group often referred to as <a href="/wiki/Macanese_people" title="Macanese people">Macanese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2006_by-census_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-2006_by-census-107">[103]</a></sup> According to the 2006 by-census, 47% of the residents were born in mainland China, of whom 74.1% were born in <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> and 15.2% in <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>. Meanwhile, 42.5% of the residents were born in Macau, and those born in Hong Kong, the Philippines and Portugal shared 3.7%, 2.0% and 0.3% respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2006_by-census_107-2"><a href="#cite_note-2006_by-census-107">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>The growth of population in Macau mainly relies on immigrants from mainland China and the influx of overseas workers since its birth rate is one of the lowest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[105]</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Factbook</a></i>, Macau has the fourth highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy</a> in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-life_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-life-15">[11]</a></sup> while its <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_infant_mortality_rate" title="List of countries by infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> ranks among the lowest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Macau's official languages are <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[108]</a></sup> Macau still retains its own dialect of Portuguese, called <a href="/wiki/Macanese_Portuguese" title="Macanese Portuguese">Macanese Portuguese</a>. Other languages—such as <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Min_Nan" title="Min Nan">Hokkien</a>—are spoken by local communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MO_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-MO-113">[109]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macanese_language" title="Macanese language">Macanese language</a>, a distinctive <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole</a> generally known as <i>Patuá</i>, is still spoken by several dozen Macanese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since Macau has an economy driven by tourism, 14.6% of the workforce is employed in restaurants and hotels, and 10.3% in the gambling industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MO_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-MO-113">[109]</a></sup> With the opening of several casino resorts and other major constructions underway, many sectors reportedly experience a shortage of labour, and the government seeks to import labour from neighbouring regions.</p>
<p>The number of imported workers stood at a record high of 98,505 in the second quarter of 2008, representing more than 25% of the labour force in Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pstat_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-pstat-115">[111]</a></sup> Some local workers complain about the lack of jobs due to the influx of cheap imported labour. Some also claim that the problem of illegal labour is severe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[112]</a></sup> Another concern is the widening of income inequality in the region. Macau's <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a>, a popular measure of income inequality where a low value indicates a more equal income distribution, rose from 0.43 in 1998 to 0.48 in 2006. It is higher than those of neighbouring regions, such as <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> (0.447), <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (0.316) and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> (0.425).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[113]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo,_Macao,_2013-08-08,_DD_44.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3167" data-file-width="4322" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_44.jpg/220px-Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_44.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_44.jpg/330px-Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_44.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_44.jpg/440px-Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_44.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo,_Macao,_2013-08-08,_DD_44.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ruins_of_St._Paul%27s" title="Ruins of St. Paul's">Ruins of St. Paul's</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Macau" title="Religion in Macau">Religion in Macau</a></div>
<p>Macau residents are endowed with considerable religious tolerance and freedom. Most Chinese in Macau are profoundly influenced by their own tradition and culture. While most are not religiously affiliated, many take part in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">Chinese folk religion</a> (<a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_2007_Yearbook_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_2007_Yearbook-61">[57]</a></sup> According to a survey conducted in 2005, 2007 and 2009, 55% of the population do not declare religious affiliation, 30% follows folk faiths, 10% are adherents of Buddhism or Taoism, and the remaining 5% part are Christians .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stats2009_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-stats2009-119">[115]</a></sup> Most Christians in Macao are members of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, which is organized and structured in Macau in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Macau" title="Diocese of Macau">Diocese of Macau</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UM_Hengqin_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2560" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/UM_Hengqin_2.jpg/220px-UM_Hengqin_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/UM_Hengqin_2.jpg/330px-UM_Hengqin_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/UM_Hengqin_2.jpg/440px-UM_Hengqin_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UM_Hengqin_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/University_of_Macau" title="University of Macau">University of Macau</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Macau" title="Education in Macau">Education in Macau</a></div>
<p>A fifteen-year free education is currently being offered to residents, that includes a three-year kindergarten, followed by a six-year primary education and a six-year secondary education. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> of the territory is 93.5%. The illiterates are mainly among the senior residents aged 65 or above; the younger generation, for example the population aged 15–29, has a literacy rate of above 99%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2006_by-census_107-3"><a href="#cite_note-2006_by-census-107">[103]</a></sup> Currently, there is only one school in Macau where Portuguese is the medium of instruction, <a href="/wiki/Macau_Portuguese_School" title="Macau Portuguese School">Macau Portuguese School</a>.</p>
<p>Macau does not have its own region-wide education system; non-tertiary schools follow either the British, the Chinese, or the Portuguese education system. There are currently 10 tertiary educational institutions in the region, four of them being public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_2007_Yearbook_61-3"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_2007_Yearbook-61">[57]</a></sup> In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a>, a worldwide test of 15-year-old schoolchildren's scholastic performance coordinated by <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>, ranked Macau as the fifth and sixth in science and problem solving respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-120">[116]</a></sup> Nevertheless, educational attainment in Macau is relatively low when compared to other high income countries. According to the 2006 by-census, among the resident population aged 14 and above, only 51.8% has a secondary education and 12.6% has a tertiary education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2006_by-census_107-4"><a href="#cite_note-2006_by-census-107">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>As prescribed by the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Basic_Law" title="Macau Basic Law">Basic Law of Macau</a> Chapter VI Article 121, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Macau" title="Government of Macau">Government of Macau</a> shall, on its own, formulate policies on education, including policies regarding the educational system and its administration, the language of instruction, the allocation of funds, the <a href="/wiki/Test_(assessment)" title="Test (assessment)">examination</a> system, the recognition of educational qualifications, and the system of academic awards so as to promote educational development. The government shall also in accordance with law, gradually institute a <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_education" title="Compulsory education">compulsory education</a> system. Community organizations and individuals may, in accordance with law, run educational undertakings of various kinds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLM_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-BLM-105">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Macau" title="List of hospitals in Macau">List of hospitals in Macau</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kiang_Wu_Hospital.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kiang_Wu_Hospital.jpg/220px-Kiang_Wu_Hospital.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kiang_Wu_Hospital.jpg/330px-Kiang_Wu_Hospital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kiang_Wu_Hospital.jpg/440px-Kiang_Wu_Hospital.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kiang_Wu_Hospital.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kiang Wu Hospital</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Macau is served by one major public hospital, the <a href="/wiki/Hospital_Conde_S._Janu%C3%A1rio" title="Hospital Conde S. Januário">Hospital Conde S. Januário</a>, and one major private hospital, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hospital_Kiang_Wu" title="Hospital Kiang Wu">Hospital Kiang Wu</a>, both located in Macau Peninsula, as well as a university associated hospital called <a href="/wiki/Macau_University_of_Science_and_Technology_Hospital" title="Macau University of Science and Technology Hospital">Macau University of Science and Technology Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cotai" title="Cotai">Cotai</a>. In addition to hospitals, Macau also has numerous health centres providing free basic medical care to residents. Consultation in <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_medicine" title="Traditional Chinese medicine">traditional Chinese medicine</a> is also available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>None of the Macau hospitals are independently assessed through <a href="/wiki/International_healthcare_accreditation" title="International healthcare accreditation">international healthcare accreditation</a>. There are no western-style medical schools in Macau, and thus all aspiring physicians in Macau have to obtain their education and qualification elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macau_2007_Yearbook_61-4"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_2007_Yearbook-61">[57]</a></sup> Local nurses are trained at the Macau Polytechnic Institute and the Kiang Wu <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">Nursing</a> College.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[119]</a></sup> Currently there are no training courses in <a href="/wiki/Midwifery" title="Midwifery">midwifery</a> in Macau.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A study by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Macau" title="University of Macau">University of Macau</a>, commissioned by the Macau SAR government, concluded that Macau is too small to have its own medical specialist training centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yaupatients_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yaupatients-124">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Macau Corps of Firefighters</i> (Portuguese: <i>Corpo de Bombeiros de Macau</i>) is responsible for ambulance service (Ambulância de Macau). The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Macau_Red_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Macau Red Cross (page does not exist)">Macau Red Cross</a> also operates ambulances (<a href="/wiki/Toyota_HiAce" title="Toyota HiAce">Toyota HiAce</a> vans) for emergency and non-emergencies to local hospitals with volunteer staff. The organization has a total of 739 uniformed firefighters and paramedics serving from 7 stations in Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Health Bureau in Macau is mainly responsible for coordinating the activities between the public and private organizations in the area of <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a>, and assure the health of citizens through specialized and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_health_care" title="Primary health care">primary health care</a> services, as well as disease prevention and <a href="/wiki/Health_promotion" title="Health promotion">health promotion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[122]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Macau_Centre_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Macau Centre for Disease Control and Prevention">Macau Centre for Disease Control and Prevention</a> was established in 2001, which monitors the operation of hospitals, health centres, and the <a href="/wiki/Blood_transfusion" title="Blood transfusion">blood transfusion</a> centre in Macau. It also handles the organization of care and prevention of diseases affecting the population, sets guidelines for hospitals and private healthcare providers, and issues <a href="/wiki/Medical_license" title="Medical license">licences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Macau healthcare authorities send many patients to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Mary_Hospital,_Hong_Kong" title="Queen Mary Hospital, Hong Kong">Queen Mary Hospital</a> in Hong Kong in certain cases, and many Macau residents intentionally seek healthcare in Hong Kong because they place more trust in Hong Kong doctors than in Mainland-trained doctors operating in Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yaupatients_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yaupatients-124">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Macau" title="Transport in Macau">Transport in Macau</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Air_Macau_Airbus_A321-200_B-MCA_(24311327220).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2561" data-file-width="3615" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Air_Macau_Airbus_A321-200_B-MCA_%2824311327220%29.jpg/220px-Air_Macau_Airbus_A321-200_B-MCA_%2824311327220%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Air_Macau_Airbus_A321-200_B-MCA_%2824311327220%29.jpg/330px-Air_Macau_Airbus_A321-200_B-MCA_%2824311327220%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Air_Macau_Airbus_A321-200_B-MCA_%2824311327220%29.jpg/440px-Air_Macau_Airbus_A321-200_B-MCA_%2824311327220%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<a href="/wiki/Air_Macau" title="Air Macau">Air Macau</a> Airbus A321</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011%E6%BE%B3%E9%97%A8%E6%B8%B8%E8%89%87%E5%B1%95%E5%B1%95%E4%BC%9A%E7%8E%B0%E5%9C%BA%E8%A7%82%E4%BC%97%E5%A6%82%E7%BB%87.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/2011%E6%BE%B3%E9%97%A8%E6%B8%B8%E8%89%87%E5%B1%95%E5%B1%95%E4%BC%9A%E7%8E%B0%E5%9C%BA%E8%A7%82%E4%BC%97%E5%A6%82%E7%BB%87.JPG/220px-2011%E6%BE%B3%E9%97%A8%E6%B8%B8%E8%89%87%E5%B1%95%E5%B1%95%E4%BC%9A%E7%8E%B0%E5%9C%BA%E8%A7%82%E4%BC%97%E5%A6%82%E7%BB%87.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/2011%E6%BE%B3%E9%97%A8%E6%B8%B8%E8%89%87%E5%B1%95%E5%B1%95%E4%BC%9A%E7%8E%B0%E5%9C%BA%E8%A7%82%E4%BC%97%E5%A6%82%E7%BB%87.JPG/330px-2011%E6%BE%B3%E9%97%A8%E6%B8%B8%E8%89%87%E5%B1%95%E5%B1%95%E4%BC%9A%E7%8E%B0%E5%9C%BA%E8%A7%82%E4%BC%97%E5%A6%82%E7%BB%87.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/2011%E6%BE%B3%E9%97%A8%E6%B8%B8%E8%89%87%E5%B1%95%E5%B1%95%E4%BC%9A%E7%8E%B0%E5%9C%BA%E8%A7%82%E4%BC%97%E5%A6%82%E7%BB%87.JPG/440px-2011%E6%BE%B3%E9%97%A8%E6%B8%B8%E8%89%87%E5%B1%95%E5%B1%95%E4%BC%9A%E7%8E%B0%E5%9C%BA%E8%A7%82%E4%BC%97%E5%A6%82%E7%BB%87.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

2011 Macau Yacht Fair</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_Ciencia,_Macao,_2013-08-08,_DD_08.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="5551" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Centro_de_Ciencia%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_08.jpg/220px-Centro_de_Ciencia%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Centro_de_Ciencia%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_08.jpg/330px-Centro_de_Ciencia%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Centro_de_Ciencia%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_08.jpg/440px-Centro_de_Ciencia%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_08.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ponte_de_Amizade" title="Ponte de Amizade">Ponte de Amizade</a> (Friendship Bridge) from <a href="/wiki/Macau_Peninsula" title="Macau Peninsula">Macau Peninsula</a> (left) to <a href="/wiki/Taipa" title="Taipa">Taipa</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macau_International_Airport_04.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1254" data-file-width="2230" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Macau_International_Airport_04.jpg/220px-Macau_International_Airport_04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Macau_International_Airport_04.jpg/330px-Macau_International_Airport_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Macau_International_Airport_04.jpg/440px-Macau_International_Airport_04.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macau_International_Airport_04.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Terminal of <a href="/wiki/Macau_International_Airport" title="Macau International Airport">Macau International Airport</a> (left) and a section of the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Light_Rail_Transit" title="Macau Light Rail Transit">LRT</a> (right)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Macau, traffic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_hand_drive" title="Left hand drive">drives on the left</a>, unlike in either mainland China or Portugal, but like neighbouring Hong Kong. Macau has a well-established public transport network connecting the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Peninsula" title="Macau Peninsula">Macau Peninsula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotai" title="Cotai">Cotai</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipa_Island" title="Taipa Island">Taipa Island</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coloane_Island" title="Coloane Island">Coloane Island</a>. Buses and taxis are the major modes of public transport in Macau. Currently three companies – <a href="/wiki/Transmac" title="Transmac">Transmac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transportas_Companhia_de_Macau" title="Transportas Companhia de Macau">Transportas Companhia de Macau</a> and Macau Nova Era de Autocarros Públicos operate franchised public bus services in Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[124]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trishaw" title="Trishaw">trishaw</a>, a hybrid of the tricycle and the rickshaw, is also available, though it is mainly for sightseeing purposes. The newest public bus operator, Macau Nova Era, previously Reolian Public Transport Co., entered service on 1 August 2011. This new bus operator operates on the existing routes by Transmac and Transportas Companhia de Macau. Free Casino Shuttle Buses are everywhere in Macau. Due to tourism being the main economic industry in Macau a majority of the larger hotels provide free round trip shuttle bus services which cover the major tourist sites including the airport, Outer Harbour Ferry Terminal, Taipa Temporary Ferry Terminal and other sites. Some Larger hotels such as Venetian Hotel and Holiday Inn even provide a free shuttle between them. The frequency for each route is usually 15 minutes.</p>
<p>The taxi system is noted for having a notoriously poor reputation among tourists and even locals. Common complaints include "constant overcharging, refusal of passengers when the destination or passenger type does not suit the driver, circuitous routes and even violent behaviour."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[125]</a></sup> In recent years, the Macau government have been making attempts to hold drivers to a higher standard of service through methods such as undercover police prosecuting drivers who violate the taxi regulations on the spot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outer_Harbour_Ferry_Terminal,_Macau" title="Outer Harbour Ferry Terminal, Macau">The Outer Harbour Ferry Terminal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Taipa_Temporary_Ferry_Terminal" title="Taipa Temporary Ferry Terminal">Taipa Temporary Ferry Terminal</a> provides cross-border transportation services for passengers travelling between Macau and Hong Kong, while the Yuet Tung Terminal in the Inner Harbour serves those travelling between Macau and cities in mainland China, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shekou_Industrial_Zone" title="Shekou Industrial Zone">Shekou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <b>Macau Light Rapid Transit</b> or <b>Macau LRT</b> also known as <b>Metro Ligeiro de Macau</b> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_transit_system" title="Mass transit system">mass transit system</a> in Macau under construction. It will serve the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Peninsula" title="Macau Peninsula">Macau Peninsula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taipa" title="Taipa">Taipa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cotai" title="Cotai">Cotai</a>, serving major border checkpoints such as the <a href="/wiki/Portas_do_Cerco" title="Portas do Cerco">Border Gate</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outer_Harbour_Ferry_Terminal,_Macau" title="Outer Harbour Ferry Terminal, Macau">Outer Harbour Ferry Terminal</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lotus_Bridge" title="Lotus Bridge">Lotus Bridge</a> Border and the <a href="/wiki/Macau_International_Airport" title="Macau International Airport">Macau International Airport</a>. It is planned to open in 2019.</p>
<p>Macau has one active international airport, known as <a href="/wiki/Macau_International_Airport" title="Macau International Airport">Macau International Airport</a> located at the eastern end of Taipa and neighbouring waters. The airport used to serve as one of the main transit hubs for passengers travelling between mainland China and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, but now with the introduction of direct flights between those two regions, passenger traffic in this regard has lessened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[129]</a></sup> It is the primary hub for <a href="/wiki/Air_Macau" title="Air Macau">Air Macau</a>. In 2006, the airport handled about 5 million passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="boilerplate metadata plainlinks" id="tfd" style="background-color: transparent; padding: 0; font-size:x-small; color:#000000; text-align: center; position: relative; float: right; border-bottom: 1px solid #AAAAAA; width: 27em">‹ The <a href="/wiki/Help:Template" title="Help:Template">template</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Template:Infobox_UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="Template:Infobox UNESCO World Heritage Site">Infobox UNESCO World Heritage Site</a></i> is being <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Templates_for_discussion/Log/2017_November_1#Template:Infobox_UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="Wikipedia:Templates for discussion/Log/2017 November 1">considered for deletion</a>. ›</div>

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Macau" title="Culture of Macau">Culture of Macau</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo,_Macao,_2013-08-08,_DD_05.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3090" data-file-width="3372" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_05.jpg/220px-Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_05.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_05.jpg/330px-Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_05.jpg/440px-Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo%2C_Macao%2C_2013-08-08%2C_DD_05.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Restos_de_la_Catedral_de_San_Pablo,_Macao,_2013-08-08,_DD_05.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Remains of the Cathedral of St. Paul, Macau</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The mixing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Culture_of_China" title="Culture of China">Chinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Portuguese cultures</a> and religious traditions for more than four centuries has left Macau with an inimitable collection of holidays, festivals and events. The biggest event of the year is the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Grand_Prix" title="Macau Grand Prix">Macau Grand Prix</a> in November,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[131]</a></sup> when the main streets in Macau Peninsula are converted to a racetrack bearing similarities with the <a href="/wiki/Monaco_Grand_Prix" title="Monaco Grand Prix">Monaco Grand Prix</a>. Other annual events include Macau Arts festival in March, the International Fireworks Display Contest in September, the International Music festival in October and/or November, and the Macau International Marathon in December.</p>
<p>The Lunar <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a> is the most important traditional festival and celebration normally takes place in late January or early February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-136">[132]</a></sup> The Pou Tai Un Temple in Taipa is the place for the Feast of Tou Tei, the Earth god, in February. The Procession of the Passion of Our Lord is a well-known Roman Catholic rite and journey, which travels from Saint Austin's Church to the Cathedral, also taking place in February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asiarooms_71-3"><a href="#cite_note-Asiarooms-71">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>A-Ma Temple, which honours the Goddess <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mazu_(goddess)" title="Mazu (goddess)">Matsu</a>, is in full swing in April with many worshippers celebrating the A-Ma festival. In May it is common to see dancing dragons at the Feast of the Drunken Dragon and twinkling-clean Buddhas at the Feast of the Bathing of Lord Buddha. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coloane_Village" title="Coloane Village">Coloane Village</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoist" title="Taoist">Taoist</a> god <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tam_Kong" title="Tam Kong">Tam Kong</a> is also honoured on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asiarooms_71-4"><a href="#cite_note-Asiarooms-71">[67]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Boat_Festival" title="Dragon Boat Festival">Dragon Boat festival</a> is brought into play on Nam Van Lake in June and Hungry Ghosts' festival, in late August and/or early September every year. All events and festivities of the year end with <a href="/wiki/Dongzhi_Festival" title="Dongzhi Festival">Winter Solstice</a> in December.</p>
<p>Macau preserves many historical properties in the urban area. The <a href="/wiki/Historic_Centre_of_Macau" title="Historic Centre of Macau">Historic Centre of Macau</a>, which includes some twenty-five historic locations, was officially listed as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> UNESCO on 15 July 2005 during the 29th session of the <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Committee" title="World Heritage Committee">World Heritage Committee</a>, held in <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a>, South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[133]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Local cooking in Macau consists of a blend of <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_cuisine" title="Cantonese cuisine">Cantonese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_cuisine" title="Portuguese cuisine">Portuguese</a> cuisines. Many unique dishes resulted from the spice blends that the wives of Portuguese sailors used in an attempt to replicate European dishes. Its ingredients and seasonings include those from Europe, South America, Africa, India, and Southeast Asia, as well as local Chinese ingredients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[134]</a></sup> Typically, Macanese food is seasoned with various spices and flavours including <a href="/wiki/Turmeric" title="Turmeric">turmeric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bacalhau" title="Bacalhau">bacalhau</a>, giving special aromas and tastes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[135]</a></sup> Famous dishes include minchi, capella, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galinha_%C3%A0_Portuguesa" title="Galinha à Portuguesa">galinha à Portuguesa</a>, galinha à Africana (African chicken), <a href="/wiki/Bacalhau" title="Bacalhau">bacalhau</a>, Macanese chili shrimps and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stir-fry" title="Stir-fry">stir-fry</a> curry crab. <a href="/wiki/Pork_chop_bun" title="Pork chop bun">Pork chop bun</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ginger_milk" title="Ginger milk">ginger milk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egg_tart" title="Egg tart">Portuguese-style egg tart</a> are also very popular in Macau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[136]</a></sup> Especially from Lord Stow's Bakery in Coloane where the first Macau-style egg tart was invented (a blend of British and Portuguese styles).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stanley_Ho" title="Stanley Ho">Stanley Ho</a>, business magnate, father of Macau gambling industry</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xian_Xinghai" title="Xian Xinghai">Xian Xinghai</a> (spelt as <i>Hsien Hsing-hai</i> during his era), 冼星海 musician and composer during Sino-Japanese War, known work included <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River_Cantata" title="Yellow River Cantata">Yellow River Cantata</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michelle_Reis" title="Michelle Reis">Michelle Reis</a>, Hong Kong actress and former Miss Hong Kong</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Edmund_Ho" title="Edmund Ho">Edmund Ho</a>, business leader, chief executive of Macau SAR</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jenny_Tseng" title="Jenny Tseng">Jenny Tseng</a>, 甄妮 Cantonese pop singer and actress in the 70s and 80s</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ming-Na_Wen" title="Ming-Na Wen">Ming-Na Wen</a>, 温明娜 TV and movie actress, one of the first Chinese-American actresses with a contract role</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Macau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008_Macau_F3_GP.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/2008_Macau_F3_GP.JPG/220px-2008_Macau_F3_GP.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/2008_Macau_F3_GP.JPG/330px-2008_Macau_F3_GP.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/2008_Macau_F3_GP.JPG/440px-2008_Macau_F3_GP.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008_Macau_F3_GP.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2008 <a href="/wiki/Macau_Grand_Prix" title="Macau Grand Prix">Macau F3 Grand Prix</a> in progress</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Macau has its own professional football league, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Campeonato_da_1%C2%AA_Divis%C3%A3o_do_Futebol" title="Campeonato da 1ª Divisão do Futebol">Campeonato da 1ª Divisão do Futebol</a>, where the <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Three_(Portugal)" title="Big Three (Portugal)">Big Three</a></i> professional football clubs of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> have their own branches: <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica_de_Macau" title="S.L. Benfica de Macau">S.L. Benfica de Macau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Clube_de_Macau" title="Sporting Clube de Macau">Sporting Clube de Macau</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F.C._Porto_de_Macau" title="F.C. Porto de Macau">F.C. Porto de Macau</a>. In general, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football (soccer)</a> has the greatest popularity in Macau, which has a representative international side, <a href="/wiki/Macau_national_football_team" title="Macau national football team">Macau national football team</a>. Another common sport is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rink_hockey" title="Rink hockey">rink hockey</a>, which is often practised by the Portuguese. The <a href="/wiki/Macau_national_roller_hockey_team" title="Macau national roller hockey team">national team of Macau</a> is the most powerful of Asia, always participates in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rink_Hockey_World_Championship" title="Rink Hockey World Championship">Rink Hockey World Championship</a> in B category and has many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rink_Hockey_Asian_Championship" title="Rink Hockey Asian Championship">Rink Hockey Asian Championship</a> titles. The last Championship was won in <a href="/wiki/Lishui" title="Lishui">Lishui</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Asian_Roller_Hockey_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="2016 Asian Roller Hockey Championship (page does not exist)">2016 Asian Roller Hockey Championship</a>. Macau also has a <a href="/wiki/Macau_national_basketball_team" title="Macau national basketball team">basketball team</a>, which qualified for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Basketball_Championship" title="Asian Basketball Championship">Asian Basketball Championship</a> twice.</p>
<p>The automobile racing event <a href="/wiki/Macau_Grand_Prix" title="Macau Grand Prix">Macau Grand Prix</a> is arguably the most important international sporting event in Macau, mainly with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Formula_3" title="Formula 3">Formula 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_racing" title="Motorcycle racing">motorcycle road racing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Touring_car_racing" title="Touring car racing">touring car</a> races.</p>
<p>Since 1989, Macau owns a <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred_horse_racing" title="Thoroughbred horse racing">thoroughbred horse racing</a> track called Taipa Racecourse operated by the <a href="/wiki/Macau_Jockey_Club" title="Macau Jockey Club">Macau Jockey Club</a>. The racecourse has a 15,000 seater <a href="/wiki/Grandstand" title="Grandstand">grandstand</a>.</p>

<li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Joseph Timothy Haydn (1885). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=CioAAAAAQAAJ&amp;pg=PA522" rel="nofollow"><i>Dictionary of dates, and universal reference. [With]</i></a> (18 ed.). Oxford University. p. 522. <q>MACAO (in Quang-tong, S. China) was given to the Portuguese as a commercial station in 1586 (in return for their assistance against pirates), subject to an annual tribute, which was remitted in 1863. Here Camoens composed part of the "Lusiad."</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+dates%2C+and+universal+reference.+%5BWith%5D&amp;rft.pages=522&amp;rft.edition=18&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.au=Joseph+Timothy+Haydn&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DCioAAAAAQAAJ%26pg%3DPA522&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMacau"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=AvRZAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA262" rel="nofollow"><i>The Mirror of literature, amusement, and instruction, Volume 7</i></a>. London: J. Limbird. 1845. p. 262. <q>The Chinese were obliged to restrict the commerce of Portugal to the port of Macau, in 1631. A partnership was then formed with some Chinese dealers in Canton, who were to furnish exports and take delivery of imports at Macau. This scheme did not suit the Chinese; they were dissatisfied with their partners, and speedily dissolved the connection.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Mirror+of+literature%2C+amusement%2C+and+instruction%2C+Volume+7&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pages=262&amp;rft.pub=J.+Limbird&amp;rft.date=1845&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DAvRZAAAAYAAJ%26pg%3DPA262&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMacau"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> (Princeton University).</span></li>

Macau's future as a Dutch colony seemed all but assured, since the city's ... still remained under construction and its defenders numbered only about 60 soldiers and 90 civilians, who ranged from Jesuit priests to African slaves</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Strolling+in+Macau%3A+A+Visitor%27s+Guide+to+Macau%2C+Taipa%2C+and+Coloane&amp;rft.pages=15&amp;rft.edition=illustrated&amp;rft.pub=ThingsAsian+Press&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.isbn=0-9715940-9-0&amp;rft.au=Steven+Bailey&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DLw6JYOYgjokC%26pg%3DPA15&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMacau"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Ruth Simms Hamilton, ed. (2007). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/?id=3s8VAQAAIAAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Routes of passage: rethinking the African diaspora, Volume 1, Part 1</i></a>. Volume 1 of African diaspora research. Michigan State University Press. p. 143. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-87013-632-1" title="Special:BookSources/0-87013-632-1">0-87013-632-1</a>. <q>Jan Coen, who had been sent to establish a Dutch base on the China coast, wrote about the slaves who served the Portuguese so faithfully: "It was they who defeated and drove away our people last year."</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Routes+of+passage%3A+rethinking+the+African+diaspora%2C+Volume+1%2C+Part+1&amp;rft.pages=143&amp;rft.pub=Michigan+State+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.isbn=0-87013-632-1&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3D3s8VAQAAIAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMacau"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span>(the University of California)</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Centro de Estudos Históricos Ultramarinos (1968). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/?id=8gdmAAAAMAAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Studia, Issue 23</i></a>. Centro de Estudos Históricos Ultramarinos. p. 89. <q>85, quotes a report from the Dutch governor-general, Coen, in 1623: "The slaves of the Portuguese at Macau served them so well and faithfully, that it was they who defeated and drove away from our people last year".</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Studia%2C+Issue+23&amp;rft.pages=89&amp;rft.pub=Centro+de+Estudos+Hist%C3%B3ricos+Ultramarinos.&amp;rft.date=1968&amp;rft.au=Centro+de+Estudos+Hist%C3%B3ricos+Ultramarinos&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3D8gdmAAAAMAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMacau"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span>(University of Texas)</span></li>

<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3" style="font-size:80%;">
<div><b>Note</b>: <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> is <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">claimed by the People's Republic of China</a> but administered by the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">Political status of Taiwan</a>). <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Macau</a> are claimed as provincial-level divisions, but as listed on the constitutional documents and joint declarations their statuses are better to be interpreted as first-level divisions instead.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></div>

<tr>
<th class="navbox-title" colspan="2" scope="col" style=";">
<div id="Notes" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><small>Notes</small></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em"></div>
<table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0">
<tr>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">* Indicates this city has already occurred above.<br/>
<p><sup>a</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality_of_China" title="Direct-controlled municipality of China">Direct-controlled Municipalities</a>. <sup>b</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Sub-provincial cities as provincial capitals</a>. <sup>c</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Separate state-planning cities</a>. <sup>1</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Special Economic Zone Cities</a>. <sup>2</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Coastal development cities</a>.<br/>
<sup>3</sup>Prefecture capital status established by Heilongjiang Province and not recognized by Ministry of Civil Affairs. Disputed by <a href="/wiki/Oroqen_Autonomous_Banner" title="Oroqen Autonomous Banner">Oroqen Autonomous Banner</a>, Hulunbuir, Inner Mongolia as part of it.<br/>
<sup>4</sup>Only administers islands and waters in South China Sea and have no urban core comparable to typical cities in China.<br/>
<sup>5</sup>The claimed province of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">Taiwan</a> no longer have any internal division announced by Ministry of Civil Affairs of PRC, due to lack of actual jurisdiction. See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Template:Administrative_divisions_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China">Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China</a> instead.<br/></p>
All provincial capitals are listed first in prefecture-level cities by province.</div>
</td>
